    function FPgetcookieForDFP(cookiename) {
    var cookiestring=document.cookie;
    var index1=cookiestring.indexOf(cookiename);
    if (index1==-1 || cookiename=='') return '';
    var index2=cookiestring.indexOf(';',index1);
    if (index2==-1) index2=cookiestring.length;
    return unescape(cookiestring.substring(index1+cookiename.length+1,index2));
}
    function setUserBehaviour()
    {
        var i, x, y, cl = document.cookie.split(";");
        var _w18userinfo_out = {};
        var c = 0;
        for (i = 0; i < cl.length; i++) {
            x = cl[i].substr(0, cl[i].indexOf("="));
            y = cl[i].substr(cl[i].indexOf("=") + 1);
            x = x.replace(/^\s+|\s+$/g, "");
            if (x == "_w18userinfo") {
                _w18userinfo_out._w18userinfo = unescape(y);
                c = c + 1
            }
            if (c == 1) {
                break;
            }
        }
        if(c==1){
            var contact = JSON.parse(_w18userinfo_out._w18userinfo);
            for (var item in contact) {
                googletag.pubads().setTargeting(item,contact[item]);
            }
        }
    }

        $(document).ready(function(){

            $(".submenu").on("mouseover", function () {
                $('.fp-lazy-navbar').each(function(){
                    src = $(this).data("src");
                    $(this).attr("src",src);
                    src = "";
                });
            });

            $("#mobile-menu").click(function(){
                if ($("#mobile-menu .fa").hasClass("fa-bars")) {
                    $("#mobile-menu .fa").removeClass("fa-bars");
                    $("#mobile-menu .fa").addClass("fa-close");
                }else{
                    $("#mobile-menu .fa").removeClass("fa-close");
                    $("#mobile-menu .fa").addClass("fa-bars");
                }
                $("body").toggleClass("menu-open");
                $("html").toggleClass("noscroll");
            });
        })

        $(window).on('DOMContentLoaded load resize scroll', function () {

            var images = $(".fp-lazy");
            // load images that have entered the viewport
            $(images).each(function (index) {
                if (isElementInViewport(this) && $(this).data("src") != '') {
                    $(this).attr("src",$(this).attr("data-src"));
                    $(this).removeAttr("data-src");
                    $(this).removeClass('fp-lazy');
                }
            })
            // if all the images are loaded, stop calling the handler
            /*if (images.length == 0) {
             $(window).off('DOMContentLoaded load resize scroll')
             }*/
        })

        function isElementInViewport (el) {

            var rect = el.getBoundingClientRect();

            return (
                    rect.top >= 0 &&
                    rect.left >= 0 &&
                    rect.bottom <= $(window).height() &&
                    rect.right <= $(window).width()
            );
        }

        $("#searchDropDown").on('click',function(){
            setTimeout(function() {
                $("#searchDropDownInput").focus();
            }, 100);

        });

        /*----------  Smooth scroll to anchor  ----------*/
        $("#go-to-top").on('click',function(e) {
            var $anchor = $(this);
            $('html,body').stop().animate({
                scrollTop: $($anchor.attr('href')).offset().top
            }, 500);
            event.preventDefault();
        });

        });


        $('.table-striped tr').click(function(){

  Latest updates:  We do not know when they were killed, could be six months back or two years back, in any case search for bodies would have begun only after the liberation of Mosul which happened in July, Swaraj said.

 Thirty-nine Indians kidnapped by the Islamic State in Iraq's Mosul in 2014 are dead, External Affairs Minister Sushma Swaraj said on Tuesday. 
 The minister told the Rajya Sabha that their bodies were spotted using deep penetration radar. The bodies were exhumed from mass graves and their identities confirmed by DNA tests, she said. 
   File image of External Affairs Minister Sushma Swaraj. PTI  
 The bodies were sent to Baghdad for DNA testing. The DNA of 38 Indians have been matched, she said. 
 All of them were construction workers, mostly from Punjab, and were employed by an Iraqi company in Mosul. 
 They were taken hostage by Islamic State militants when they took control of the second largest city in Iraq in 2014. The workers were trying to leave Mosul when they were held hostage. 
 Minister of State for External Affairs VK Singh visited Iraq, days after Mosul was liberated by Iraqi forces from the rule of Islamic State. 
 In July 2017, after ruckus in the Lok Sabha over the issue of the 39 Indians missing in Mosul, Swaraj said that there is no evidence to substantiate the claim that they have died. And declaring anyone dead without proof is a sin that I won't commit, she had said. 
 Earlier, the Punjab Congress had accused the external affairs minister of misleading the country on the fate of missing Indians abducted in Iraq, and asked her to provide credible information on the issue.

                                                                                <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320182355" class="clearfix">
                            <span>18:23</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Informing families through television unpardonable, says Omar Abdullah</strong></p>



<p>National Conference leader Omar Abdullah took to Twitter to criticise the way the government handled this issue. He said, "Senior people in MEA, if not the Minister and&nbsp;her junior minister themselves, should have spoken to each of the 39 families before the news of the deaths was made public."</p>




                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320180253" class="clearfix">
                            <span>18:02</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Intelligence agencies knew of deaths in 2014; Govt waited for liberation before announcement</strong></p>



<p>Mosul was declared liberated from the Islamic State in July 2017. A month later, when Indian officials arrived, they found that 39 Indians taken hostage by the terrorists of the so-called caliphate were missing. The Indian authorities were informed about mass graves in Badush, a village northwest of Mosul, which had a prison cell operated by the Islamic State terrorists.</p>



<p>A missive was sent to New Delhi, which contacted the state government to arrange DNA samples of family members of 39 missing Indians. The process was finally completed with the help of respective district magistrates in October- November 2017.</p>



<p><a href="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-intelligence-agencies-knew-of-deaths-in-2014-govt-waited-for-mosul-liberation-before-announcement-4398017.html?google_editors_picks=true"><em>Read the full article here</em></a></p>


                        </a>
                    </li>

                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320174824" class="clearfix">

                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320174536" class="clearfix">
                            <span>17:45</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Captain Amarinder Singh writes to Swaraj, seeks financial aid for kin of deceased</strong></p>






                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320173914" class="clearfix">
                            <span>17:39</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Congress flays govt for 'misleading' kin of those killed, Surjewala says Swaraj should apologise to each and every family</strong></p>






                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320173119" class="clearfix">
                            <span>17:31</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Faced with tragedy, family members reveal agents, employers duped people on promise of well-paying jobs</strong></p>



<p>Nishan Singh was a crane operator and had been working in Dubai since 2011. In 2013 his employer put two options before him that either he should go back home as there was no work in Dubai or he should go and work in Iraq.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Given the volatile situation in Iraq, initially, Nishan was hesitant to go but due to the &lsquo;attractive salary&rsquo; being offered to him, he left for Mosul. Only once he could send Rs 20,000 back home to his parents but after that it stopped, as he himself failed to get the salary promised to him, which was Rs 40,000. The family of Nishan Singh visited Delhi several times and even met Minister for External Affairs, Sushma Swaraj. Except assurances, they got nothing.&nbsp;</p>



<p>&ldquo;My brother told us that his employer never gave him the salary promised that was to him. Whatever he used to get got spent on food. He was in a very deplorable state over there. A person who has no means to earn his livelihood here in Punjab, goes to Dubai and Middle East for a job,&rdquo; added Sarvan, who finally broke into tears.&nbsp;</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320172758" class="clearfix">
                            <span>17:27</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Aman&nbsp;Kumar's family paid Rs 1 lakh to agent to get him job in Iraq</strong></p>



<p>Aman Kumar from Kangra district in Himachal Pradesh left for Mosul in 2013. The family paid Rs 1 lakh to an agent from Kharar, Chandigarh. Aman was a high school dropout and used to operate heavy construction vehicles and was getting paid Rs 50,000 a month in Iraq. His brother Raman Kumar told <em>Firstpost</em> that the family is in deep shock but doesn't want to comment further at the moment.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320170315" class="clearfix">
                            <span>17:03</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>'Nishan Singh wanted to come back home after war broke out'</strong></p>



<p>Despite being a witness to bomb blasts, constant firings and dead bodies of unknown people lying scattered on the streets of Mosul in northern Iraq, 32-year old Nishan Singh a native of Sangoana village in Punjab couldn&rsquo;t return to India as his employer insisted him to stay back and work.</p>



<p>"My elder brother used to call us from Mosul and tell us about the dangerous situation over there. We asked him to come back, but he said that his employer had insisted to continue working for another seven months, so it won&rsquo;t be possible for him. Since 2014, we failed to hear anything from him and had been waiting for his comeback, which ultimately didn&rsquo;t happen. Now after waiting for so long we&rsquo;ve been told about his death,"&nbsp;Sarwan Singh (30), younger brother of Nishan Singh told <em>Firstpost.</em></p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320165449" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:54</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>'External affairs ministry never said he was dead,' Surjit&nbsp;Mainka's&nbsp;family</strong></p>



<p>Surjit Mainka's 7-year-old son holds up a photograph of his father, who was one of the 39 Indians killed by Islamic State in Iraq. He was a carpenter and was failing to make ends meet in Chuharwali village in Jalandhar, Punjab. Surjit's brother-in-law Manjeet told <em>Firstpost</em> that an agent had charged nearly Rs 2.5 lakh to fly Surjit to Iraq.</p>



<p>"When he left for Iraq in 2013, there was peace and during the first nine months of his stay there, everything was fine,"&nbsp;said Manjeet. He along with Surjit's wife used to attend meetings with the external affairs ministry in Delhi since June 2014, when they last established contact with him. They were hoping the promises Sushma Swaraj was making all this while meant something. But now after learning about his death&nbsp;they feel betrayed.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320164556" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:45</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>'We feel cheated by the govt, they kept shifting stance,' says Madan&nbsp;Lal's&nbsp;family</strong></p>



<p>Madan Lal left for Mosul in 2013 from Qadian, Gurdaspur district in Punjab. His parents work as labourers and they took a loan of Rs 4 lakh to pay an agent from Jalandhar who had promised their son a decent job in Iraq.</p>



<p>When Madan Lal reached Mosul, he started working as a gate keeper. The family last spoke to him in June 2014. His older brother Deepak told <em>Firstpost</em> that he had been to Delhi thrice since 2014 and alleged that the External Affairs ministry had been misleading him on his brother's whereabouts. In those meetings, he alleged that they repeatedly changed their stance and convinced him that the 20 something boy was fine and was working in a factory. He said his family feels cheated by the government and wants the prime minister to explain why this has happened to young men who left the country in search for better opportunities. He said the family may be inconsolable right now but will fight this battle for justice and demand answers from the people in power.&nbsp;</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320164222" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:42</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Issue is being politicised, we want DNA reports: Kin of&nbsp;Manjinder Singh</strong></p>



<p>"We demand from the government to provide us DNA reports. The issue is being politicised. We had been running from pillar to post since last four years and&nbsp;now we're being told via TV that we lost one of our own," Gurpinder Kaur, sister of Manjinder Singh told&nbsp;<em><a href="https://twitter.com/ANI/status/976050924727783424">ANI</a>.&nbsp;</em></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320163027" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:30</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Didn't keep anybody in dark, waiting for concrete proof was protocol: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>"I didn't keep anybody in dark but there is a difference between a government and an individual. Harjeet Singh (the lone survivor amid the Indians in Mosul) was a person and could have said anything. As a government, officiating his version of events merited some responsibility. We believed in putting in efforts to first ascertain that there is absolutely no scope that our people could be alive, only then we channeled our energies in looking for bodies." Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320162447" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:24</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Bodies weren't found in mass graves, recovered during Gen (retd) VK Singh's visit</strong></p>



<p>"I would like to clarify that our people were not found in any mass grave but the bodies were recovered from under a mound. The first sign was that the bodies were exactly 39 in number, plus strands of long hair and a kada was found. So we started conducting DNA tests. the Martyr's Mission completed their formalities and decided to announce the deaths today, I told the House about it before their&nbsp;press conference," Swaraj said.</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320161542" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:15</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Harjeet Masih&nbsp;was not harassed: Sushma Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>"It is baseless that Harjit Masih was harassed, he was kept in protective custody. I had said this in Parliament earlier," Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320161344" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:13</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Don't know when the 39 Indians were killed: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>"We do not know when they were killed,&nbsp;could be six months back or two years back, in any case search for bodies would have begun only after the liberation of Mosul which happened in July,"&nbsp;Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320161024" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:10</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Those dead hail from 4 states; We will try to bring back bodies as soon as possible: Sushma Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>Speaking to the press, Sushma&nbsp;Swaraj said that 27 of the people were from Punjab, 4 from Himachal&nbsp;Pradesh, 6 from Bihar and 2 from West Bengal. One person whose DNA has matched 70 percent with the samples is from Bihar.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She said that the next logical conclusion would to grant closure to the families by bringing the bodies back. "I have asked the High Commission to fast track the process to bring the bodies back so that the family members can at least hold funeral rituals and grieve their dead," Swaraj said.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320160050" class="clearfix">
                            <span>16:00</span> (IST) <br/><p><span style="color:#FF0000"><strong>DNA samples of 38 people have been matched, verification of one&nbsp;victim is under process: Sushma Swaraj</strong></span></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320155904" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:59</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>'Didn't betray anyone, this was tireless effort, not falsehood,' says&nbsp;Sushma Swaraj&nbsp;</strong></p>



<p>"I had told the House continuously for three years that until I get proof of their death, I will not close any file. It would have been a sin had we handed over anybody's body claiming it to be those of our people, just for the sake of closing file."&nbsp;</p>



<p>"We had been saying that we neither have the evidence of them being alive nor the evidence of them being dead. We maintained this in 2014 and 2017. We did not keep anyone in dark," Swaraj said.&nbsp;She quoted her own statements from the House and said, "this wasn't falsehood, this was a tireless effort."</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320155520" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:55</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Told Parliament first because of House was in Session, kept my word: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>"Some kin of the victims have questioned as to why they were not told about the deaths before the parliament. It is parliamentary procedure to first inform the house, so it was my duty," Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She also said that she had said on the floor of the Upper House that she would tell the Parliament as soon as she learns about the fate of the missing Indians.&nbsp;</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320155023" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:50</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>We did everything we could to find the missing Indians: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>Sushma Swaraj said that the government did all it could to find the missing Indians. "We reached out to every diplomatic channel that could have helped us in getting any clue to the location or the state of the missing Indians," Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She also said that the government could not have declared the missing Indians dead in haste. "There are some governments that believe in the concept of 'missing believed to be dead', but we were stern that I won't close their files until and unless I get concrete proofs," Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320154426" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:44</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Sushma Swaraj slams Congress for disrupting House proceedings</strong></p>



<p>"Will we play politics even on people's death?" Swaraj asked. She said that she had spoken to the agitating members and taken their assurance that they will not create noise, even though they refused to vacate the Well. "But today, Congress was leading the protests and Jyotiraditya&nbsp;Scindia was leading the Congress members," she said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She slammed the Congress members for playing "politics over the death of 39 Indians."</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320153950" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:39</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Wanted to inform Parliament on slain Indians: Sushma&nbsp;Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>"I had called the press before speaking in Parliament because of the current mood of the Houses. But when I spoke to Venkaiah ji he told me that he is sure the members will understand the gravity of the issue. And members in the Rajya Sabha valued that request," Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320153603" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:36</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Sushma Swaraj briefs the press</strong></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320153108" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:31</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>We tried hard to convince him not to go to Iraq: Manjeet&nbsp;Singh, Davinder&nbsp;Singh's wife</strong></p>



<p>Davinder Singh (52)&nbsp;left for Mosul to work at the Erbil Steel company in November 2011, a year after his twin sons were born. His wife Manjeet Kaur spoke to <em>Firstpost</em> and said Davinder was the only earning member in the family and she had been desperately waiting to hear back from the external affairs ministry since 15 June 2014,&nbsp;when she had spoken to him the last time.</p>



<p>The family tried its best to stop him from going to Iraq but he was unemployed and desperate for a job in India. Manjeet said that Davinder's sisters had also came to Jalandhar to convince him to change his mind about moving to Iraq. Manjeet&nbsp;revealed that even in Iraq, her husband wasn't making more than Rs 25,000 a month. Davinder is survived by a wife and three sons. &nbsp;</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320152530" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:25</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Govt mishandled this issue, why did EAM&nbsp;built false hopes, asks Shashi Tharoor</strong></p>

<p><strong>​</strong></p>

<p>Congress leader Shahsi Tharoor, speaking to media persons outside Parliament, said that the government has mishandled a very sensitive issue. "Why did the government still kept saying with such conviction that those people were alive," Tharoor&nbsp;asked.&nbsp;</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320152029" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:20</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Amarinder Singh 'shattered' over development, AAP asks Sushma Swaraj to resign</strong></p>



<p>Punjab chief minister Captain Amarinder Singh on Tuesday said he was "shattered at the heart-wrenching news" that 39 Indians, kidnapped by the Islamic State, had been killed in Iraq.</p>



<p>His Congress colleague Partap Singh Bajwa and Aam Aadmi Party's Kanwar Sandhu also expressed their grief and targeted External Affairs Minister Sushma Swaraj for misleading the families of those who had died.&nbsp;Sandhu also asked for the minister's resignation.</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320151634" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:16</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Govt kept saying they were all right: Wife of Gurcharan Singh</strong></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320151459" class="clearfix">
                            <span>15:14</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Family members hold government responsible for building false hope</strong></p>



<p>Parminder Lucky who lost two of his &nbsp;family members in Iraq says that the pain of losing them is unbearable for his family. "Kawaljit Singh was my brother and Gurdeep Singh(32) was my brother in law. Both went to Iraq for years ago and kept in touch till June 2014. Suddenly they stopped calling home," Parminder said.</p>



<p>"The Ministry of External Affairs kept telling us that they will return. But suddenly they have said the people are no more," lamented Parminder.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;</p>

<p>Gurdeep Singh is survived by his wife and two daughters, four years and 5 years old.&nbsp;On the other hand Kawaljeet Singh has left behind his wife and a five year old daughter.</p>


                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320144945" class="clearfix">
                            <span>14:49</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>We don't demand anything from the govt, says one of the family members of the deceased</strong></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320142501" class="clearfix">
                            <span>14:25</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Shocked to hear that 39 Indians are now confirmed dead: Rahul Gandhi</strong></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320140546" class="clearfix">
                            <span>14:05</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Two of the deceased were promised salary of Rs 35,000-40,000 per month in Iraq</strong></p>

<p>Santosh&nbsp;Kumar (29) and&nbsp;Vidhya&nbsp;Bhushan&nbsp;(35)&nbsp;Tiwari&nbsp;left for Mosul from&nbsp;Sahasraon&nbsp;village in Bihar's&nbsp;Siwan&nbsp;district in 2011.</p>

<p>They were both matriculates and decided to give up studying and look for&nbsp;labour&nbsp;jobs in West Asia.</p>

<p>Santosh's&nbsp;brother&nbsp;Pappu&nbsp;Kumar shared that the two zeroed in on Iraq together because the opportunity was lucrative and an agent from&nbsp;Uttar&nbsp;Pradesh convinced them that violence had lessened.</p>

<p>Both the two were also promised around Rs 35,000-40,000 per month.</p>

<p>Vidhya&nbsp;Bhushan&nbsp;Tiwari's&nbsp;uncle&nbsp;Purshottam&nbsp;Tiwari&nbsp;shared that his nephew had worked in a steel plant in&nbsp;Bokaro. The two were working as pipe-fitters in industrial pockets in Mosul.</p>

<p>In 2014, the two were held hostage.&nbsp;Pappu&nbsp;Kumar shared that the families met&nbsp;Sushma&nbsp;Swaraj last year and she had told them that 39 Indians had been held hostage. The families had been hoping this year would bring them some relief.</p>

<p>(In the photo:&nbsp;Santosh&nbsp;Kumar)</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320133510" class="clearfix">
                            <span>13:35</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Govt was giving us false promises: Kin of deceased</strong></p>

<p>Dimplejeet, sister of Dharminder Kumar (one of the deceased), said the government tried to mislead the families all along.</p>

<p>Dharminder, a resident of Batala, Gurdaspurm, was among the 39 Indians kidnapped by the Islamic State in Mosul. After Sushma Swaraj informed the Parliament on Tuesday that all 39 Indians are dead, Dimplejeet told <em>Firstpost</em> the family is heart-broken.</p>

<p>"The government was giving us false promises everytime we met them. Even recently, we were told that nothing happened to Dharminder and he would be home soon. What was the need to lie to us? the government should have been little more sympathetic to us. We wanted him back,&rdquo; Dimplejeet said.</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320131638" class="clearfix">
                            <span>13:16</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>I have been saying what Sushma Swaraj said for three years: Mosul kidnapping survivor</strong></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320131143" class="clearfix">
                            <span>13:11</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>List of the deceased identified so far</strong></p>

<p><em>Firstpost</em> was able to access a list of 27 deceased who have been identified so far. Of these, 22 were from Punjab, three from Himachal Pradesh and two from Bihar.</p>

<p><a href="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-by-islamic-state-in-iraqs-mosul-list-of-names-of-27-deceased-identified-so-far-4397543.html"><strong>Click here to view the list of the names of 27 deceased identified so far.</strong></a></p>
                        </a>
                    </li>
                                                                                                    <li>
                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320130657" class="clearfix">
                            <span>13:06</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>Sushma Swaraj had said that until there is strong proof, she will not inform the House: VK Singh</strong></p>

<p>"There was hope, but then seeing the situation there, chances of them being alive seemed slim. Legal procedures are underway there and might take 8-10 days. We are waiting for them to complete," ANI further quoted Singh as saying.</p>

<p>On the Opposition leaders' remarks, Singh said, "It is the job of the Opposition to take things the wrong way. I do not want to say anything about it."</p>
                        </a>
                    </li>

                        <a href="#live-blog-20180320125458" class="clearfix">
                            <span>12:54</span> (IST) <br/><p><strong>This should have been announced earlier: Amarinder Singh</strong></p>

<p>"We had expected this, it should have been announced earlier, it was known since much earlier," <em>ANI</em> quoted Punjab chief minister Amarinder Singh as saying.</p>

                                                            <p class="date-time">18:23<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Informing families through television unpardonable, says Omar Abdullah</strong></p>



<p>National Conference leader Omar Abdullah took to Twitter to criticise the way the government handled this issue. He said, &quot;Senior people in MEA, if not the Minister and&nbsp;her junior minister themselves, should have spoken to each of the 39 families before the news of the deaths was made public.&quot;</p>




                                            </p>
                                                            <p class="blog-source"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en"><p lang="en" dir="ltr">Nothing Govt of India says can make up for the sheer heartlessness displayed today. Using Parliament as an excuse for the families of 39 dead Indians having to learn of their heartbreaking loss from TV channels is unpardonable.</p>&mdash; Omar Abdullah (@OmarAbdullah) <a href="https://twitter.com/OmarAbdullah/status/976051772283334656?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">March 20, 2018</a></blockquote> <script async src="https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js" charset="utf-8"></script></p>

                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320180253"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                                                                        <meta content="http://www.firstpost.com/" itemprop="sameAs">
                                                                        <meta content="firstpost.com" itemprop="name">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/FP-LiveCoverage-Box.jpg">

                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Intelligence agencies knew of deaths in 20..true"> Read the full article here   

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">18:02<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Intelligence agencies knew of deaths in 2014; Govt waited for liberation before announcement</strong></p>



<p>Mosul was declared liberated from the Islamic State in July 2017. A month later, when Indian officials arrived, they found that 39 Indians taken hostage by the terrorists of the so-called caliphate were missing. The Indian authorities were informed about mass graves in Badush, a village northwest of Mosul, which had a prison cell operated by the Islamic State terrorists.</p>



<p>A missive was sent to New Delhi, which contacted the state government to arrange DNA samples of family members of 39 missing Indians. The process was finally completed with the help of respective district magistrates in October- November 2017.</p>



<p><a href="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-intelligence-agencies-knew-of-deaths-in-2014-govt-waited-for-mosul-liberation-before-announcement-4398017.html?google_editors_picks=true"><em>Read the full article here</em></a></p>


                                            </p>

            <li class="20180320173119 " itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" itemprop="liveBlogUpdate" itemscope="itemscope">
                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320173119"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                                                                        <meta content="http://www.firstpost.com/" itemprop="sameAs">
                                                                        <meta content="firstpost.com" itemprop="name">
                                                                     </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="http://lbimg.in.com/LiveBlog/img/2018/03/3d3cab2538450e634dfa8cb551a1f450.jpeg">
                                                                        <meta content="480" itemprop="width"><meta content="267" itemprop="height">
                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Faced with tragedy, family members reveal ..d Sarvan, who finally broke into tears.&nbsp; 

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">17:31<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Faced with tragedy, family members reveal agents, employers duped people on promise of well-paying jobs</strong></p>



<p>Nishan Singh was a crane operator and had been working in Dubai since 2011. In 2013 his employer put two options before him that either he should go back home as there was no work in Dubai or he should go and work in Iraq.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Given the volatile situation in Iraq, initially, Nishan was hesitant to go but due to the &lsquo;attractive salary&rsquo; being offered to him, he left for Mosul. Only once he could send Rs 20,000 back home to his parents but after that it stopped, as he himself failed to get the salary promised to him, which was Rs 40,000. The family of Nishan Singh visited Delhi several times and even met Minister for External Affairs, Sushma Swaraj. Except assurances, they got nothing.&nbsp;</p>



<p>&ldquo;My brother told us that his employer never gave him the salary promised that was to him. Whatever he used to get got spent on food. He was in a very deplorable state over there. A person who has no means to earn his livelihood here in Punjab, goes to Dubai and Middle East for a job,&rdquo; added Sarvan, who finally broke into tears.&nbsp;</p>


                                            </p>

                        <p></p>

                                                            <p class="date-time">17:27<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Aman&nbsp;Kumar&#39;s family paid Rs 1 lakh to agent to get him job in Iraq</strong></p>



<p>Aman Kumar from Kangra district in Himachal Pradesh left for Mosul in 2013. The family paid Rs 1 lakh to an agent from Kharar, Chandigarh. Aman was a high school dropout and used to operate heavy construction vehicles and was getting paid Rs 50,000 a month in Iraq. His brother Raman Kumar told <em>Firstpost</em> that the family is in deep shock but doesn&#39;t want to comment further at the moment.&nbsp;</p>

            <li class="20180320170315 " itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" itemprop="liveBlogUpdate" itemscope="itemscope">
                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320170315"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                                                                        <meta content="http://www.firstpost.com/" itemprop="sameAs">
                                                                        <meta content="firstpost.com" itemprop="name">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/FP-LiveCoverage-Box.jpg">
                                                                        <meta content="480" itemprop="width"><meta content="267" itemprop="height">
                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  &#39;Nishan Singh wanted to come back home..ther of Nishan Singh told  Firstpost.  

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">17:03<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>&#39;Nishan Singh wanted to come back home after war broke out&#39;</strong></p>



<p>Despite being a witness to bomb blasts, constant firings and dead bodies of unknown people lying scattered on the streets of Mosul in northern Iraq, 32-year old Nishan Singh a native of Sangoana village in Punjab couldn&rsquo;t return to India as his employer insisted him to stay back and work.</p>



<p>&quot;My elder brother used to call us from Mosul and tell us about the dangerous situation over there. We asked him to come back, but he said that his employer had insisted to continue working for another seven months, so it won&rsquo;t be possible for him. Since 2014, we failed to hear anything from him and had been waiting for his comeback, which ultimately didn&rsquo;t happen. Now after waiting for so long we&rsquo;ve been told about his death,&quot;&nbsp;Sarwan Singh (30), younger brother of Nishan Singh told <em>Firstpost.</em></p>


                                            </p>

                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  &#39;External affairs ministry never said ..ng about his death&nbsp;they feel betrayed.&nbsp; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">16:54<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>&#39;External affairs ministry never said he was dead,&#39; Surjit&nbsp;Mainka&#39;s&nbsp;family</strong></p>



<p>Surjit Mainka&#39;s 7-year-old son holds up a photograph of his father, who was one of the 39 Indians killed by Islamic State in Iraq. He was a carpenter and was failing to make ends meet in Chuharwali village in Jalandhar, Punjab. Surjit&#39;s brother-in-law Manjeet told <em>Firstpost</em> that an agent had charged nearly Rs 2.5 lakh to fly Surjit to Iraq.</p>



<p>&quot;When he left for Iraq in 2013, there was peace and during the first nine months of his stay there, everything was fine,&quot;&nbsp;said Manjeet. He along with Surjit&#39;s wife used to attend meetings with the external affairs ministry in Delhi since June 2014, when they last established contact with him. They were hoping the promises Sushma Swaraj was making all this while meant something. But now after learning about his death&nbsp;they feel betrayed.&nbsp;</p>
                                            </p>

            <li class="20180320164556 " itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" itemprop="liveBlogUpdate" itemscope="itemscope">
                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320164556"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">

                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  &#39;We feel cheated by the govt, they kep..emand answers from the people in power.&nbsp; 

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">16:45<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>&#39;We feel cheated by the govt, they kept shifting stance,&#39; says Madan&nbsp;Lal&#39;s&nbsp;family</strong></p>



<p>Madan Lal left for Mosul in 2013 from Qadian, Gurdaspur district in Punjab. His parents work as labourers and they took a loan of Rs 4 lakh to pay an agent from Jalandhar who had promised their son a decent job in Iraq.</p>



<p>When Madan Lal reached Mosul, he started working as a gate keeper. The family last spoke to him in June 2014. His older brother Deepak told <em>Firstpost</em> that he had been to Delhi thrice since 2014 and alleged that the External Affairs ministry had been misleading him on his brother&#39;s whereabouts. In those meetings, he alleged that they repeatedly changed their stance and convinced him that the 20 something boy was fine and was working in a factory. He said his family feels cheated by the government and wants the prime minister to explain why this has happened to young men who left the country in search for better opportunities. He said the family may be inconsolable right now but will fight this battle for justice and demand answers from the people in power.&nbsp;</p>


                                            </p>

                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Issue is being politicised, we want DNA reports: Kin of&nbsp;Manjinder Singh</strong></p>



<p>&quot;We demand from the government to provide us DNA reports. The issue is being politicised. We had been running from pillar to post since last four years and&nbsp;now we&#39;re being told via TV that we lost one of our own,&quot; Gurpinder Kaur, sister of Manjinder Singh told&nbsp;<em><a href="https://twitter.com/ANI/status/976050924727783424">ANI</a>.&nbsp;</em></p>

                                                            <p class="date-time">16:30<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Didn&#39;t keep anybody in dark, waiting for concrete proof was protocol: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>&quot;I didn&#39;t keep anybody in dark but there is a difference between a government and an individual. Harjeet Singh (the lone survivor amid the Indians in Mosul) was a person and could have said anything. As a government, officiating his version of events merited some responsibility. We believed in putting in efforts to first ascertain that there is absolutely no scope that our people could be alive, only then we channeled our energies in looking for bodies.&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                                            </p>

                                                            <p class="date-time">16:24<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Bodies weren&#39;t found in mass graves, recovered during Gen (retd) VK Singh&#39;s visit</strong></p>



<p>&quot;I would like to clarify that our people were not found in any mass grave but the bodies were recovered from under a mound. The first sign was that the bodies were exactly 39 in number, plus strands of long hair and a kada was found. So we started conducting DNA tests. the Martyr&#39;s Mission completed their formalities and decided to announce the deaths today, I told the House about it before their&nbsp;press conference,&quot; Swaraj said.</p>

                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Don&#39;t know when the 39 Indians were ki..h happened in July,&quot;&nbsp;Swaraj said.&nbsp; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">16:13<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Don&#39;t know when the 39 Indians were killed: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>&quot;We do not know when they were killed,&nbsp;could be six months back or two years back, in any case search for bodies would have begun only after the liberation of Mosul which happened in July,&quot;&nbsp;Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                                            </p>

                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320161024"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/FP-LiveCoverage-Box.jpg">

                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">

                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Those dead hail from 4 states; We will try..grieve their dead,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;&nbsp; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">16:10<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Those dead hail from 4 states; We will try to bring back bodies as soon as possible: Sushma Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>Speaking to the press, Sushma&nbsp;Swaraj said that 27 of the people were from Punjab, 4 from Himachal&nbsp;Pradesh, 6 from Bihar and 2 from West Bengal. One person whose DNA has matched 70 percent with the samples is from Bihar.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She said that the next logical conclusion would to grant closure to the families by bringing the bodies back. &quot;I have asked the High Commission to fast track the process to bring the bodies back so that the family members can at least hold funeral rituals and grieve their dead,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                                            </p>
                                                            <p>

            <li class="20180320155904 " itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" itemprop="liveBlogUpdate" itemscope="itemscope">
                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320155904"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                                                                        <meta content="http://www.firstpost.com/" itemprop="sameAs">
                                                                        <meta content="firstpost.com" itemprop="name">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/FP-LiveCoverage-Box.jpg">
                                                                        <meta content="480" itemprop="width"><meta content="267" itemprop="height">
                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  &#39;Didn&#39;t betray anyone, this was ti..39;t falsehood, this was a tireless effort.&quot; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:59<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>&#39;Didn&#39;t betray anyone, this was tireless effort, not falsehood,&#39; says&nbsp;Sushma Swaraj&nbsp;</strong></p>



<p>&quot;I had told the House continuously for three years that until I get proof of their death, I will not close any file. It would have been a sin had we handed over anybody&#39;s body claiming it to be those of our people, just for the sake of closing file.&quot;&nbsp;</p>



<p>&quot;We had been saying that we neither have the evidence of them being alive nor the evidence of them being dead. We maintained this in 2014 and 2017. We did not keep anyone in dark,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;She quoted her own statements from the House and said, &quot;this wasn&#39;t falsehood, this was a tireless effort.&quot;</p>
                                            </p>
                                                            <p>

                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">

                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Told Parliament first because of House was.. about the fate of the missing Indians.&nbsp; 

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:55<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Told Parliament first because of House was in Session, kept my word: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>&quot;Some kin of the victims have questioned as to why they were not told about the deaths before the parliament. It is parliamentary procedure to first inform the house, so it was my duty,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She also said that she had said on the floor of the Upper House that she would tell the Parliament as soon as she learns about the fate of the missing Indians.&nbsp;</p>


                                            </p>

            <li class="20180320155023 " itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting" itemprop="liveBlogUpdate" itemscope="itemscope">
                <div itemprop="articleBody">
                    <time itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30"></time>
                    <time itemprop="url" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html#20180320155023"></time>
                    <span itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="author" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                                                                        <meta content="http://www.firstpost.com/" itemprop="sameAs">
                                                                        <meta content="firstpost.com" itemprop="name">
                                                                     </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="image">
                                                                        <meta itemprop="url" content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/FP-LiveCoverage-Box.jpg">
                                                                        <meta content="480" itemprop="width"><meta content="267" itemprop="height">
                                                                    </span>
                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  We did everything we could to find the mis..s I get concrete proofs,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:50<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>We did everything we could to find the missing Indians: Swaraj</strong></p>



<p>Sushma Swaraj said that the government did all it could to find the missing Indians. &quot;We reached out to every diplomatic channel that could have helped us in getting any clue to the location or the state of the missing Indians,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She also said that the government could not have declared the missing Indians dead in haste. &quot;There are some governments that believe in the concept of &#39;missing believed to be dead&#39;, but we were stern that I won&#39;t close their files until and unless I get concrete proofs,&quot; Swaraj said.&nbsp;</p>
                                            </p>

                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Sushma Swaraj slams Congress for disruptin..quot;politics over the death of 39 Indians.&quot; ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:44<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Sushma Swaraj slams Congress for disrupting House proceedings</strong></p>



<p>&quot;Will we play politics even on people&#39;s death?&quot; Swaraj asked. She said that she had spoken to the agitating members and taken their assurance that they will not create noise, even though they refused to vacate the Well. &quot;But today, Congress was leading the protests and Jyotiraditya&nbsp;Scindia was leading the Congress members,&quot; she said.&nbsp;</p>



<p>She slammed the Congress members for playing &quot;politics over the death of 39 Indians.&quot;</p>

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">

                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  We tried hard to convince him not to go to.. is survived by a wife and three sons. &nbsp; 

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:31<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>We tried hard to convince him not to go to Iraq: Manjeet&nbsp;Singh, Davinder&nbsp;Singh&#39;s wife</strong></p>



<p>Davinder Singh (52)&nbsp;left for Mosul to work at the Erbil Steel company in November 2011, a year after his twin sons were born. His wife Manjeet Kaur spoke to <em>Firstpost</em> and said Davinder was the only earning member in the family and she had been desperately waiting to hear back from the external affairs ministry since 15 June 2014,&nbsp;when she had spoken to him the last time.</p>



<p>The family tried its best to stop him from going to Iraq but he was unemployed and desperate for a job in India. Manjeet said that Davinder&#39;s sisters had also came to Jalandhar to convince him to change his mind about moving to Iraq. Manjeet&nbsp;revealed that even in Iraq, her husband wasn&#39;t making more than Rs 25,000 a month. Davinder is survived by a wife and three sons. &nbsp;</p>


                                            </p>

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:20<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Amarinder Singh &#39;shattered&#39; over development, AAP asks Sushma Swaraj to resign</strong></p>



<p>Punjab chief minister Captain Amarinder Singh on Tuesday said he was &quot;shattered at the heart-wrenching news&quot; that 39 Indians, kidnapped by the Islamic State, had been killed in Iraq.</p>



<p>His Congress colleague Partap Singh Bajwa and Aam Aadmi Party&#39;s Kanwar Sandhu also expressed their grief and targeted External Affairs Minister Sushma Swaraj for misleading the families of those who had died.&nbsp;Sandhu also asked for the minister&#39;s resignation.</p>

                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Family members hold government responsible..behind his wife and a five year old daughter. 

">
                                                            <p class="date-time">15:14<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Family members hold government responsible for building false hope</strong></p>



<p>Parminder Lucky who lost two of his &nbsp;family members in Iraq says that the pain of losing them is unbearable for his family. &quot;Kawaljit Singh was my brother and Gurdeep Singh(32) was my brother in law. Both went to Iraq for years ago and kept in touch till June 2014. Suddenly they stopped calling home,&quot; Parminder said.</p>



<p>&quot;The Ministry of External Affairs kept telling us that they will return. But suddenly they have said the people are no more,&quot; lamented Parminder.&nbsp;<br />
&nbsp;</p>

<p>Gurdeep Singh is survived by his wife and two daughters, four years and 5 years old.&nbsp;On the other hand Kawaljeet Singh has left behind his wife and a five year old daughter.</p>


                                            </p>

                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Ranjit Singh, one of the deceased, had talked about coming back home</strong></p>

<p>Jaspreet Kaur, sister of Ranjit Singh (one of the deceased), began crying when she talked about her brother.</p>

<p>She said that the last time she spoke to her brother was on 15 June, 2014. He had talked to her about coming back home at that time.</p>

                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/Organization" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="publisher">
                                                                        <span itemtype="https://schema.org/ImageObject" itemscope="itemscope" itemprop="logo">
                                                                            <meta content="https://images.firstpost.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/03/FP-Logo.png" itemprop="url">
                                                                        </span>
                                                                        <meta content="Firstpost" itemprop="name">
                                                                    </span>
                    <meta itemprop="mainEntityOfPage" content="http://www.firstpost.com/india/39-indians-killed-in-mosul-news-updates-punjab-cm-condoles-demise-of-those-killed-by-islamic-state-4397531.html">
                    <meta itemprop="dateModified" content="2018-03-21T09:17:00+05:30">
                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Govt didn&#39;t give us time: Kin of decea..tance on the veracity of Harjeet&#39;s statement. ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">14:32<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Govt didn&#39;t give us time: Kin of deceased</strong></p>

<p>A few months after Malkit Singh was married in February 2014, he left for Iraq for a job.</p>

<p>But he fell prey to the bad conditions in Iraq. He died after being held by the Islamic State.</p>

<p>Speaking to <em>Firstpost</em>, Malkit Singh&#39;s brother Manjit said that even though they had asked the government for time, no one from the government met any of them.</p>

<p>He said that the government kept changing its statement. Manjit cannot believe that his brother is no longer in this world. &quot;Until the government presents strong proof, we will not accept this,&quot; he said.</p>

<p>He is also angry with the statement of Harjeet, one of the 40 Indians who escaped. He said that the government also changed its stance on the veracity of Harjeet&#39;s statement.</p>
                                            </p>

                                        <meta itemprop="headline" content="  Kawaljit Singh&#39;s death came as a shock..rdaspur, along with his old parents and siblings. ">
                                                            <p class="date-time">14:09<span> (IST)</span></p>
                    
                                        <p>
                                                <p><strong>Kawaljit Singh&#39;s death came as a shock for the family</strong></p>

<p>Kawaljit Singh (35), who went to Iraq four years ago, was kidnapped by terrorists just after he reached there.</p>

<p>His family members were still hoping that he will return one day. Angrej Singh, his nephew, told <em>Firstpost</em> that the news of his death came as a shock for the family. He is survived by his wife and 5-year-old daughter in his home in Gurdaspur, along with his old parents and siblings.</p>
                                            </p>
